i like the bulk write for mongo and the batch calls to get the fixture data, but im getting the feeling that we dont even need the subflow called "fixtures_flow_monitor"
in fact id like to do a huge restructure and i want you to remove anything thats no longer needed really, although the docker things should be set up well for the code changes

we're going to use 2 flows for our project:
fixtures_flow
twitter_flow

we're going to use 2 tasks for fixtures_flow:
fixtures_ingest
fixtures_monitor

we're going to have 2 helper methods for fixtures_flow:
fixtures_advance (source and destination collection as parameters)
goal_trigger (fixture id as parameter)

we're going to use 1 task for twitter_flow:
twitter_advance (source and destination collection as parameters)

we're going to use 6 mongodb collections for our project:
teams
fixtures_staging
fixtures_active
fixtures_processed
goals_active
goals_processed

(when i speak below and speak about time just know im of course speaking about date and time not literally the current time on a clock)
(when i speak about goals i am only talking about non penalty shootout goals, although normal penalties are good)

fixtures_flow will be started by fixtures-flow-daily and fixtures-flow-manual as we have been doing but now the fixtures_flow will trigger task fixtures_ingest

flow fixtures_flow:
- calls task fixtures_ingest
- starts scheduled task fixtures_monitor once every 3 minutes after fixtures_ingest is completed (should run once right away after fixtures_ingest is completed and then every 3 minutes after)

task fixtures_ingest:
- calls API to retrieve all fixtures for a certain date
- iterates over fixtures and ingests data into fixtures_staging and fixtures_active based on certain conditions
    - fixtures which do not contain a team in our teams collection (based on id) are ignored
    - fixtures which have a start time after the current time will be added to fixtures_staging and a task fixtures_advance is scheduled for 5 minutes prior to the match start time with the parameters fixtures_staging and fixtures_active
    - fixtures which have a start time before the current time will be added to collection fixtures_active, and event goal_trigger is triggered for that goal event

task fixtures_monitor:
- started in fixtures flow as a scheduled task meant to run every minute after fixtures_ingest has completed until collections fixtures_staging and fixtures_active are empty
- makes a batch API call to get data about all fixtures in collection fixtures_active
- does a diff of the API data against the existing fixtures in collection fixtures_active to see if any new goals have occured (have the total number of goals home + away increased), in which case event goal_trigger is started called for those goal events
- updates existing fixtures after goal_trigger is called for all goal events

task fixtures_advance (source and destination collection as parameters)
- copies fixture data from source collection to destination collection, while removing that data from the source collection

task goal_trigger
- fetches goal data from API and stores it in collection goals_active (primary key should be the fixture id and minute the goal occurred)
- triggers twitter_flow for that goal event (goals_active primary key)

flow twitter_flow:
- calls task twitter_advance (goals_active and goals_processed as parameters)
- calls task fixtures_advance (fixtures_active and fixtures_processed as parameters)

below are some api call and return examples (one above the other), any methods created to access them should share the exact same name as the endpoint (after the /v3/):

import requests

url = "https://api-football-v1.p.rapidapi.com/v3/fixtures"

querystring = {"date":"2021-04-07"}

headers = {
	"x-rapidapi-key": "3815c39f56msh68991ec604f7be3p1cb7c4jsnf78a6cb47415",
	"x-rapidapi-host": "api-football-v1.p.rapidapi.com"
}

response = requests.get(url, headers=headers, params=querystring)

print(response.json())
